00260   template <typename T>
00261   concept concurrent_hash_map =
00262       hash_map<T> &&
00263       requires(
00264           const T& cinstance, T& instance,
00265           std::add_lvalue_reference_t<std::add_const_t<typename T::key_type>>
00266                                key,
00267           helpers::visit_dummy func,
00268           std::add_lvalue_reference_t<std::add_const_t<typename T::value_type>>
00269                                                         val,
00270           std::initializer_list<typename T::value_type> list) {
00271         {
00272           cinstance.visit(key, func)
00273         } -> std::same_as<size_t>;
00274         {
00275           cinstance.cvisit(key, func)
00276         } -> std::same_as<size_t>;
00277         {
00278           cinstance.visit_all(func)
00279         } -> std::same_as<size_t>;
00280         {
00281           cinstance.cvisit_all(func)
00282         } -> std::same_as<size_t>;
00283         {
00284           instance.insert(val)
00285         } -> std::same_as<bool>;
00286         {
00287           instance.insert(list)
00288         };
00289         {
00290           instance.insert_or_visit(val, func)
00291         } -> std::same_as<bool>;
00292         {
00293           instance.insert_or_cvisit(val, func)
00294         } -> std::same_as<bool>;
00295         {
00296           cinstance.max_load()
00297         } -> std::same_as<typename T::size_type>;
00298       };

00300   template <typename T>
00301   concept regular_hash_map =
00302       hash_map<T> && forward_iterable<T> &&
00303       requires(
00304           const T& cinstance, T& instance,
00305           std::add_lvalue_reference_t<std::add_const_t<typename T::value_type>>
00306                                                         val,
00307           typename T::iterator                          itr,
00308           std::initializer_list<typename T::value_type> list,
00309           std::add_lvalue_reference_t<std::add_const_t<typename T::mapped_type>>
00310               obj,
00311           std::add_lvalue_reference_t<std::add_const_t<typename T::key_type>>
00312                                      key,
00313           typename T::const_iterator citr) {
00314         {
00315           instance.insert(val)
00316         } -> std::same_as<std::pair<typename T::iterator, bool>>;
00317         instance.insert(itr, itr);
00318         instance.insert(list);
00319         {
00320           instance.insert_or_assign(key, obj)
00321         } -> std::same_as<std::pair<typename T::iterator, bool>>;
00322         {
00323           instance.insert_or_assign(citr, key, obj)
00324         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::iterator>;
00325         {
00326           instance.erase(citr)
00327         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::iterator>;
00328         {
00329           instance.erase(key)
00330         } -> std::same_as<typename T::size_type>;
00331         instance.swap(instance);
00332         instance.clear();
00333         instance.merge(instance);
00334         {
00335           instance.find(key)
00336         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::iterator>;
00337         {
00338           cinstance.find(key)
00339         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::const_iterator>;
00340         {
00341           instance.equal_range(key)
00342         }
00343         -> std::same_as<std::pair<typename T::iterator, typename T::iterator>>;
00344         {
00345           cinstance.equal_range(key)
00346         } -> std::same_as<
00347             std::pair<typename T::const_iterator, typename T::const_iterator>>;
00348         instance.at(key) = obj;
00349         instance[key]    = obj;
00350       };
00351 
00352   template <typename T>
00353   concept multi_hash_map =
00354       hash_map<T> && forward_iterable<T> &&
00355       requires(
00356           T& instance, const T& cinstance, const typename T::value_type& val,
00357           std::initializer_list<typename T::value_type> list,
00358           typename T::iterator itr, typename T::const_iterator citr,
00359           const typename T::key_type& key, const typename T::mapped_type& obj) {
00360         instance.insert(itr, itr);
00361         instance.insert(list);
00362         {
00363           instance.erase(citr)
00364         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::iterator>;
00365         {
00366           instance.erase(key)
00367         } -> std::same_as<typename T::size_type>;
00368         instance.swap(instance);
00369         instance.clear();
00370         instance.merge(instance);
00371         instance.merge(instance);
00372         {
00373           instance.find(key)
00374         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::iterator>;
00375         {
00376           cinstance.find(key)
00377         } -> std::convertible_to<typename T::const_iterator>;
00378         {
00379           instance.equal_range(key)
00380         }
00381         -> std::same_as<std::pair<typename T::iterator, typename T::iterator>>;
00382         {
00383           cinstance.equal_range(key)
00384         } -> std::same_as<
00385             std::pair<typename T::const_iterator, typename T::const_iterator>>;
00386       };

00388   template <typename T>
00389   concept closed_addressing =
00390       (regular_hash_map<T> || multi_hash_map<T>)&&requires(
00391           T& instance, const T& cinstance, typename T::size_type n,
00392           const typename T::key_type& key) {
00393         typename T::local_iterator;
00394         typename T::const_local_iterator;
00395         {
00396           instance.begin(n)
00397         } -> std::same_as<typename T::local_iterator>;
00398         {
00399           instance.end(n)
00400         } -> std::same_as<typename T::local_iterator>;
00401         {
00402           cinstance.begin(n)
00403         } -> std::same_as<typename T::const_local_iterator>;
00404         {
00405           cinstance.end(n)
00406         } -> std::same_as<typename T::const_local_iterator>;
00407         {
00408           cinstance.cbegin(n)
00409         } -> std::same_as<typename T::const_local_iterator>;
00410         {
00411           cinstance.cend(n)
00412         } -> std::same_as<typename T::const_local_iterator>;
00413         {
00414           cinstance.max_bucket_count()
00415         } -> std::same_as<typename T::size_type>;
00416         {
00417           cinstance.bucket_size(n)
00418         } -> std::same_as<typename T::size_type>;
00419         {
00420           cinstance.bucket(key)
00421         } -> std::same_as<typename T::size_type>;
00422       };

00878   template <typename... types>

00886 
00887   namespace helpers
00888   {
00889     template <typename seq>
00890     inline constexpr bool detours_and_originals_impl = false;
00891 
00892     template <typename tuple, typename... rest>
00893     inline constexpr bool
00894         detours_and_originals_impl<type_sequence<tuple, rest...>> =
00895             callable_type<std::tuple_element_t<0, tuple>> &&
00896             function_type<std::tuple_element_t<1, tuple>> &&
00897             std::is_lvalue_reference_v<std::tuple_element_t<1, tuple>> &&
00898             detours_and_originals_impl<type_sequence<rest...>>;
00899 
00900     template <typename first, typename second, typename... rest>
00901     inline constexpr bool detours_and_originals_impl<
00902         type_sequence<type_sequence<first, second>, rest...>> =
00903         callable_type<first> && function_type<second> &&
00904         std::is_lvalue_reference_v<second> &&
00905         detours_and_originals_impl<type_sequence<rest...>>;
00906 
00907     template <>
00908     inline constexpr bool detours_and_originals_impl<type_sequence<>> = true;
00909 
00910     template <typename key, typename seq>
00911     inline constexpr bool keys_detours_and_originals_impl = false;
00912 
00913     template <typename key, typename tuple, typename... rest>
00914     inline constexpr bool
00915         keys_detours_and_originals_impl<key, type_sequence<tuple, rest...>> =
00916             std::is_convertible_v<std::tuple_element_t<0, tuple>, key> &&
00917             callable_type<std::tuple_element_t<1, tuple>> &&
00918             function_type<std::tuple_element_t<2, tuple>> &&
00919             std::is_lvalue_reference_v<std::tuple_element_t<2, tuple>> &&
00920             keys_detours_and_originals_impl<key, type_sequence<rest...>>;
00921 
00922     template <typename key, typename first, typename second, typename third,
00923               typename... rest>
00924     inline constexpr bool keys_detours_and_originals_impl<
00925         key, type_sequence<type_sequence<first, second, third>, rest...>> =
00926         std::is_convertible_v<first, key> && callable_type<second> &&
00927         function_type<third> && std::is_lvalue_reference_v<third> &&
00928         keys_detours_and_originals_impl<key, type_sequence<rest...>>;
00929 
00930     template <typename key>
00931     inline constexpr bool
00932         keys_detours_and_originals_impl<key, type_sequence<>> = true;

00991   template <typename detour, typename original, typename... rest>
00992   concept detours_and_originals =
00993       !pair_like_types<detour, original, rest...> &&
00994       (sizeof...(rest) % 2) == 0 &&
00995       helpers::detours_and_originals_impl<
00996           make_type_pairs_t<detour, original, rest...>>;
00997 
00998   template <typename key, typename detour, typename original, typename... rest>
00999   concept keys_detours_and_originals =
01000       !tuple_like_types<key, detour, original, rest...> &&
01001       (sizeof...(rest) % 3) == 0 &&
01002       helpers::keys_detours_and_originals_impl<
01003           key, make_type_triplets_t<key, detour, original, rest...>>;
01004 
01005   template <typename pair, typename... rest>
01006   concept detour_and_original_pairs =
01007       pair_like_types<pair, rest...> &&
01008       helpers::detours_and_originals_impl<
01009           type_sequence<remove_cvref_t<pair>, remove_cvref_t<rest>...>>;
01010 
01011   template <typename tuple, typename... rest>
01012   concept key_detour_and_original_triplets =
01013       fixed_tuple_like_types<3, tuple, rest...> &&
01014       helpers::keys_detours_and_originals_impl<
01015           std::tuple_element_t<0, remove_cvref_t<tuple>>,
01016           type_sequence<remove_cvref_t<tuple>, remove_cvref_t<rest>...>>;
01017

00049   /**
00050    * @brief Takes a function-like type and defines a function type of the form
00051    * of `ret(args...)` where `ret` is the return type of the function passed and
00052    * `args...` its argument types respectively.
00053    * @tparam T the function-like type to use. Can be a function type, a regular
00054    * function pointer, a member function pointer or an instance of
00055    * `std::function`.
00056    * @note This also handles stuff like calling conventions, constness and the
00057    * noexcept specifier. Therefore it can come in handy when in need to simplify
00058    * partial overloads. Also note that for member function pointers, it adds the
00059    * implicit `this` pointer as a first argument with its expected constness.

00108   /**
00109    * @brief Takes any type and evaluates to true if `T` meets the requirements
00110    * of a captureless lambda.
00111    * @tparam T the type to check
00112    *
00113    * The requirements for `T` to be considered as a captureless lambda are:
00114    * - It must have a non-ambiguous overload of `operator()` defined. (because
00115    * of this generic lambdas are not allowed)
00116    * - Must be implicitly convertible to its respective function pointer via an
00117    * overload of `operator F()`.
00118    */
00119   template <typename T>
00120   concept captureless_lambda = requires(T instance) {
00121     &T::operator();
00122     typename clean_function_type_t<decltype(&T::operator())>;
00123     static_cast<std::add_pointer_t<helpers::remove_first_arg_t<
00124         clean_function_type_t<decltype(&T::operator())>>>>(instance);
00125   };
00126

00130

00132   /**
00133    * @brief Takes a captureless lambda type and defined the function type to
00134    * which it can be implicitly converted.
00135    * @tparam T the capturless lambda to use
00136    * @note On 32-bit windows this also minds calling convention tags (e.g.
00137    * `utils::fastcall`). As a result it will proceed to replace the tags with
00138    * their respective calling convention on the type defined. If you are
00139    * interested in the actual underlying function type to which the lambda can
00140    * be converted, a second typedef is provided named `actual_type` that keeps
00141    * the tags in the return type and still include their respective calling
00142    * convention! One exception to be note is lambdas tagged with
00143    * `utils::thiscall` in which case the old tag will be replaced by a different
00144    * implementation tag and no calling convention will be added. The reason
00145    * being the MSVC doesn't like `__thiscall` used on function types.
00146    */
00147   template <typename T>
00148   struct captureless_lambda_func_type
00149       : helpers::captureless_lambda_clean_type_impl<decltype(&T::operator())>
00150   {
00151   };
00152 
00153   /// Alias for @ref alterhook::utils::captureless_lambda_func_type
00154   template <typename T>
00155   using capturless_lambda_func_type_t =
00156       typename captureless_lambda_func_type<T>::type;
00157 
00158   /// Alias for @ref alterhook::utils::captureless_lambda_func_type but uses the
00159   /// other typedef instead
00160   template <typename T>
00161   using captureless_lambda_actual_func_type_t =
00162       typename captureless_lambda_func_type<T>::actual_type;

00164   /**
00165    * @brief Removes constness and references via `remove_cvref_t` on any type
00166    * passed. On function pointers it calls `std::remove_pointer_t` to get back a
00167    * function type and on capturless lambdas it uses
00168    * `captureless_lambda_func_type` to get the underlying function type of the
00169    * lambda.
00170    * @tparam T the type to use (can be anything).
00171    * @note On 32-bit windows when `T` is a function pointer with the
00172    * `__thiscall` calling convention the result type is a function type with
00173    * same args and specifiers but with the return type replaced by a custom
00174    * internal tag that denotes the said calling convention. The reason for doing
00175    * this is that MSVC does not accept function types with this calling
00176    * convention applied.
00177    */
00178   template <typename T>
00179   struct clean_type : helpers::clean_type_impl<remove_cvref_t<T>>
00180   {
00181   };

00184   template <typename T>

00187   /**
00188    * @brief Takes any type and evaluates to true when `T` is a function
00189    * type/pointer, a member function pointer or an instance of `std::function`,
00190    * false otherwise.
00191    * @tparam T the type to use (can be anything).
00192    * @note constness and references are removed before checking.

00287   /**
00288    * @brief Checks if the arguments of `fn_1` are compatible with those of
00289    * `fn_2`.
00290    * @tparam fn_1 the first callable type to use
00291    * @tparam fn_2 the second callable type to use
00292    *
00293    * On platforms other than 32-bit windows this basically just checks if the
00294    * arguments of both are identical. On 32-bit windows however, calling
00295    * conventions are taken into account. So for example when you want to
00296    * determine compatibility between a `__fastcall` and a `__thiscall` function,
00297    * this concept requires that the `__fastcall` function has an additional
00298    * argument placed after the first one that is of size equal to
00299    * `sizeof(void*)` and is unused. The rest of arguments of `__fastcall` should
00300    * be identical to those of `__thiscall` (and in the same order). Now if the
00301    * first template parameter is the one with `__thiscall` and not the second it
00302    * instead requires that both accept only one argument and that it's the same
00303    * one.
00304    */
00305   template <typename fn_1, typename fn_2>
00306    concept  compatible_function_arguments_with =
00307       helpers::have_compatible_fn_args<fn_1, fn_2>();
00308

00310   template <typename T>

00529     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00530      concept  are_member_function_pointers =
00531         std::is_member_function_pointer_v<T1> &&
00532         std::is_member_function_pointer_v<T2>;
00533     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00534      concept  has_any_mem_func_ptr =
00535         std::is_member_function_pointer_v<T1> ||
00536         std::is_member_function_pointer_v<T2>;
00537 
00538     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00539      concept  are_pointers = std::is_pointer_v<T1> && std::is_pointer_v<T2>;
00540 
00541     template <typename PT1, typename PT2,
00542               typename T1 = std::remove_pointer_t<PT1>,
00543               typename T2 = std::remove_pointer_t<PT2>>
00544      concept  have_this =
00545         are_pointers<PT1, PT2> &&
00546         (std::is_base_of_v<T1, T2> ||
00547          std::is_base_of_v<T2, T1>)&&same_cv_qualification_v<T1, T2>;

00549     template <typename seq, typename fn_1, typename fn_2>
00550     inline constexpr bool all_arguments_same_check =
00551         undefined_struct<seq, fn_1, fn_2>::value;
00552     template <size_t... indexes, typename fn_1, typename fn_2>
00553     inline constexpr bool
00554         all_arguments_same_check<std::index_sequence<indexes...>, fn_1, fn_2> =
00555             (std::is_same_v<fn_argument_t<fn_1, indexes>,
00556                             fn_argument_t<fn_2, indexes - 1>> &&
00557              ...);
00558 
00559     template <typename seq, typename fn_1, typename fn_2, bool member_fn>
00560     inline constexpr bool all_arguments_same_check_2_impl =
00561         undefined_struct<seq, fn_1, fn_2>::value;
00562     // handles case where either detour or original is member function (we need
00563     // to check if the first arg with is the this pointer is of type that has
00564     // any relationship with the other one and have equal size)
00565     template <size_t index, size_t... indexes, typename fn_1, typename fn_2>
00566     inline constexpr bool all_arguments_same_check_2_impl<
00567         std::index_sequence<index, indexes...>, fn_1, fn_2, true> =
00568         have_this<remove_cvref_t<fn_argument_t<fn_1, index>>,
00569                   remove_cvref_t<fn_argument_t<fn_2, index>>> &&
00570         (std::is_same_v<fn_argument_t<fn_1, indexes>,
00571                         fn_argument_t<fn_2, indexes>> &&
00572          ...);
00573     template <size_t... indexes, typename fn_1, typename fn_2>
00574     inline constexpr bool all_arguments_same_check_2_impl<
00575         std::index_sequence<indexes...>, fn_1, fn_2, false> =
00576         (std::is_same_v<fn_argument_t<fn_1, indexes>,
00577                         fn_argument_t<fn_2, indexes>> &&
00578          ...);
00579 
00580     template <typename seq, typename fn_1, typename fn_2>
00581     inline constexpr bool all_arguments_same_check_2 =
00582         all_arguments_same_check_2_impl<seq, fn_1, fn_2,
00583                                         has_any_mem_func_ptr<fn_1, fn_2>>;

00586     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00587     concept have_compatible_member_fn_first_args =
00588         requires {
00589           typename fn_argument_t<T1, 0>;
00590           typename fn_argument_t<T2, 0>;
00591         } && have_this<std::remove_cvref_t<fn_argument_t<T1, 0>>,
00592                        std::remove_cvref_t<fn_argument_t<T2, 0>>>;
00593 
00594     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00595     concept have_all_args_same =
00596         fn_arity_v<T1> == fn_arity_v<T2> &&
00597         all_arguments_same_check_2<std::make_index_sequence<fn_arity_v<T1>>, T1,
00598                                    T2>;

00626     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00627     concept have_all_fastcall_args_compatible_with_thiscall =
00628         have_compatible_member_fn_first_args<T1, T2> &&
00629         requires { typename fn_argument_t<T1, 1>; } &&
00630         sizeof(fn_argument_t<T1, 1>) == sizeof(void*) &&
00631         fn_arity_v<T2> == (fn_arity_v<T1> - 1) &&
00632         all_arguments_same_check<make_index_sequence_t<fn_arity_v<T1>, 2>, T1,
00633                                  T2>;

00648     /*
00649      * on windows x86 verify that arguments are compatible
00650      * that means for example if you are trying to hook a thiscall function of
00651      * arity greater than 1 with a fastcall one you should include an argument
00652      * of size == sizeof(void*) as a second argument to avoid issues. on other
00653      * platforms we just check that all arguments are identical, no calling
00654      * convention headache for them
00655      */
00656     template <typename T1, typename T2>
00657      consteval  bool have_compatible_fn_args()
00658     {
00659 
00660 
00661 
00662 
00663 
00664 
00665 
00666 
00667 
00668 
00669 
00670 
00671 
00672 
00673 
00674 
00675 
00676 
00677 
00678 
00679 
00680       return have_all_args_same<T1, T2>;
00681 
00682     }

00327     template <typename T, size_t N>
00328     class static_vector_iterator : public static_vector_const_iterator<T, N>
00329     {
00330     public:
00331       typedef static_vector_const_iterator<T, N> base;
00332 
00333       typedef std::contiguous_iterator_tag iterator_concept;
00334 
00335       typedef std::random_access_iterator_tag iterator_category;
00336       typedef T                               value_type;
00337       typedef ptrdiff_t                       difference_type;
00338       typedef T*                              pointer;
00339       typedef T&                              reference;
00340 
00341       constexpr static_vector_iterator() noexcept {}
00342 
00343 
00344       constexpr explicit static_vector_iterator(pointer       ptr,
00345                                                 const size_t* size = nullptr,
00346                                                 size_t offset      = 0) noexcept
00347           : base(ptr, size, offset)
00348       {
00349       }
00350 
00351 
00352 
00353 
00354 
00355 
00356 
00357 
00358       constexpr reference operator*() const noexcept
00359       {
00360         return const_cast<reference>(base::operator*());
00361       }
00362 
00363       constexpr pointer operator->() const noexcept
00364       {
00365         return const_cast<pointer>(base::operator->());
00366       }
00367 
00368       constexpr static_vector_iterator& operator++() noexcept
00369       {
00370         base::operator++();
00371         return *this;
00372       }
00373 
00374       constexpr static_vector_iterator operator++(int) noexcept
00375       {
00376         static_vector_iterator tmp = *this;
00377         base::operator++();
00378         return tmp;
00379       }
00380 
00381       constexpr static_vector_iterator& operator--() noexcept
00382       {
00383         base::operator--();
00384         return *this;
00385       }
00386 
00387       constexpr static_vector_iterator operator--(int) noexcept
00388       {
00389         static_vector_iterator tmp = *this;
00390         base::operator--();
00391         return tmp;
00392       }
00393 
00394       constexpr static_vector_iterator&
00395           operator+=(const ptrdiff_t offset) noexcept
00396       {
00397         base::operator+=(offset);
00398         return *this;
00399       }
00400 
00401       constexpr static_vector_iterator
00402           operator+(const ptrdiff_t offset) const noexcept
00403       {
00404         static_vector_iterator tmp  = *this;
00405         tmp                        += offset;
00406         return tmp;
00407       }
00408 
00409       friend constexpr static_vector_iterator
00410           operator+(const ptrdiff_t offset, static_vector_iterator itr) noexcept
00411       {

00413         return itr;
00414       }
00415 
00416       constexpr static_vector_iterator&
00417           operator-=(const ptrdiff_t offset) noexcept
00418       {
00419         base::operator-=(offset);
00420         return *this;
00421       }
00422 
00423       using base::operator-;
00424

00426           operator-(const ptrdiff_t offset) const noexcept
00427       {

00429         tmp                        -= offset;
00430         return tmp;
00431       }
00432 
00433       constexpr reference operator[](const ptrdiff_t offset) const noexcept
00434       {
00435         return const_cast<reference>(base::operator[](offset));
00436       }
00437 
00438     private:
00439

00441       friend struct std::pointer_traits;
00442 
00443       template <typename U, size_t M>
00444       friend class utils::static_vector;

00446       constexpr pointer unwrap() const noexcept
00447       {
00448         return const_cast<pointer>(base::unwrap());
00449       }
00450     };

00452 
00453   template <typename T, size_t N>
00454   class static_vector
00455   {
00456   private:
00457     std::aligned_storage_t<sizeof(T), alignof(T)> data[N];
00458     size_t                                        count = 0;
00459 
00460     static void verify_len(size_t len, const char* str)
00461     {
00462       if (len > N)
00463       {
00464         std::stringstream stream{};
00465         stream << "static_vector: " << str << " > this->size() <=> " << len
00466                << " > " << N;
00467         throw(std::length_error(stream.str()));
00468       }
00469     }
00470 
00471   public:
00472     typedef T                                           value_type;
00473     typedef size_t                                      size_type;
00474     typedef ptrdiff_t                                   difference_type;
00475     typedef T*                                          pointer;
00476     typedef const T*                                    const_pointer;
00477     typedef T&                                          reference;
00478     typedef const T&                                    const_reference;
00479     typedef T&&                                         rvalue_reference;
00480     typedef helpers::static_vector_iterator<T, N>       iterator;
00481     typedef helpers::static_vector_const_iterator<T, N> const_iterator;
00482     typedef std::reverse_iterator<iterator>             reverse_iterator;
00483     typedef std::reverse_iterator<const_iterator>       const_reverse_iterator;
00484 
00485     // none of the bellow is marked as constexpr simply because c++ malds when
00486     // reinterpret_cast is being used at compile time. use an actual vector if
00487     // you want compile time behaviour, this is meant for runtime performance
00488     static_vector() : count() {}
00489 
00490     static_vector(std::initializer_list<T> list) : count(list.size())
00491     {
00492       verify_len(list.size(), "list.size()");
00493       std::uninitialized_copy(list.begin(), list.end(), begin().unwrap());
00494     }
00495 
00496     explicit static_vector(size_t count) : count(count)
00497     {
00498       verify_len(count, "count");
00499       std::uninitialized_value_construct(begin().unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00500     }
00501 
00502     template < std::forward_iterator  itr>
00503     static_vector(itr first, itr last) : count(std::distance(first, last))
00504     {
00505       verify_len(count, "std::distance(first, last)");
00506       std::uninitialized_copy(first, last, begin().unwrap());
00507     }
00508 
00509     static_vector(const static_vector& other) : count(other.count)
00510     {
00511       std::uninitialized_copy(other.begin().unwrap(), other.end().unwrap(),
00512                               begin().unwrap());
00513     }
00514 
00515     static_vector(static_vector&& other) : count(other.count)
00516     {
00517       std::uninitialized_move(other.begin().unwrap(), other.end().unwrap(),
00518                               begin().unwrap());
00519       other.clear();
00520     }
00521 
00522     ~static_vector() { clear(); }
00523 
00524 
00525     iterator begin() noexcept
00526     {
00527       return iterator(std::launder(reinterpret_cast<pointer>(data)), &count, 0);
00528     }
00529 
00530     const_iterator begin() const noexcept
00531     {
00532       return const_iterator(std::launder(reinterpret_cast<const_pointer>(data)),
00533                             &count, 0);
00534     }
00535 
00536     iterator end() noexcept
00537     {
00538       return iterator(std::launder(reinterpret_cast<pointer>(data)), &count,
00539                       count);
00540     }
00541 
00542     const_iterator end() const noexcept
00543     {
00544       return const_iterator(std::launder(reinterpret_cast<const_pointer>(data)),
00545                             &count, count);
00546     }

00571     reverse_iterator rbegin() noexcept { return reverse_iterator(end()); }
00572 
00573     const_reverse_iterator rbegin() const noexcept
00574     {
00575       return const_reverse_iterator(end());
00576     }
00577 
00578     reverse_iterator rend() noexcept { return reverse_iterator(begin()); }
00579 
00580     const_reverse_iterator rend() const noexcept
00581     {
00582       return const_reverse_iterator(begin());
00583     }
00584 
00585     const_iterator cbegin() const noexcept { return begin(); }
00586 
00587     const_iterator cend() const noexcept { return end(); }
00588 
00589     const_reverse_iterator crbegin() const noexcept { return rbegin(); }
00590 
00591     const_reverse_iterator crend() const noexcept { return rend(); }
00592 
00593     bool empty() const noexcept { return !count; }
00594 
00595     operator bool() const noexcept { return !empty(); }
00596 
00597     size_t size() const noexcept { return count; }
00598 
00599     constexpr size_t max_size() { return N; }
00600 
00601     constexpr size_t capacity() { return max_size(); }
00602 
00603     pointer c_array() noexcept
00604     {
00605       return std::launder(reinterpret_cast<pointer>(data));
00606     }
00607 
00608     const_pointer c_array() const noexcept
00609     {
00610       return std::launder(reinterpret_cast<const_pointer>(data));
00611     }
00612 
00613     T& operator[](size_t pos) noexcept
00614     {
00615       return *std::launder(reinterpret_cast<pointer>(&data[pos]));
00616     }
00617 
00618     const T& operator[](size_t pos) const noexcept
00619     {
00620       return *std::launder(reinterpret_cast<const_pointer>(&data[pos]));
00621     }
00622 
00623     T& at(size_t pos)
00624     {
00625       verify_len(pos, "pos");
00626       return *std::launder(reinterpret_cast<pointer>(&data[pos]));
00627     }
00628 
00629     const T& at(size_t pos) const
00630     {
00631       verify_len(pos, "pos");
00632       return *std::launder(reinterpret_cast<const_pointer>(&data[pos]));
00633     }
00634 
00635     void clear()
00636     {
00637       std::destroy(begin().unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00638       count = 0;
00639     }
00640 
00641     template <typename... types>
00642     reference emplace_back(types&&... values)
00643     {
00644       verify_len(count + 1, "(count + 1)");
00645       pointer res = new (end().unwrap()) T{ std::forward<types>(values)... };
00646       ++count;
00647       return *res;
00648     }
00649 
00650     reference push_back(const_reference value) { return emplace_back(value); }
00651 
00652     reference push_back(rvalue_reference value)
00653     {
00654       return emplace_back(std::move(value));
00655     }
00656 
00657     template <typename... types>
00658     iterator emplace(iterator where, types&&... values)
00659     {
00660       verify_len(count + 1, "(count + 1)");
00661       if (where != end())
00662       {
00663         new (end().unwrap()) T{ std::move(*(end() - 1)) };
00664         std::move_backward(where.unwrap(), (end() - 1).unwrap(),
00665                            end().unwrap());
00666         *where = T{ std::forward<types>(values)... };
00667       }
00668       else
00669         new (end().unwrap()) T{ std::forward<types>(values)... };
00670       ++count;
00671       return where;
00672     }
00673 
00674     iterator insert(iterator where, const_reference val)
00675     {
00676       return emplace(where, val);
00677     }
00678 
00679     iterator insert(iterator where, rvalue_reference val)
00680     {
00681       return emplace(where, std::move(val));
00682     }
00683 
00684     iterator insert(iterator where, const size_t insert_count,
00685                     const_reference value)
00686     {
00687       if (insert_count)
00688       {
00689         verify_len(insert_count + count, "(insert_count + count");
00690         const size_t affected_elements = end() - where;
00691         if (insert_count > affected_elements)
00692         {
00693           std::uninitialized_move(
00694               where.unwrap(), end().unwrap(),
00695               std::uninitialized_fill_n(
00696                   end().unwrap(), insert_count - affected_elements, value));
00697           std::fill(where.unwrap(), end().unwrap(), value);
00698         }
00699         else
00700         {
00701           std::uninitialized_move((end() - insert_count).unwrap(),
00702                                   end().unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00703           std::move_backward(where.unwrap(), (end() - insert_count).unwrap(),
00704                              end().unwrap());
00705           std::fill(where.unwrap(), (where + insert_count).unwrap(), value);
00706         }
00707         count += insert_count;
00708       }
00709       return where;
00710     }
00711 
00712     template < std::forward_iterator  itr>
00713     iterator insert(iterator where, itr first, itr last)
00714     {
00715       const auto len = std::distance(first, last);
00716       if (len)
00717       {
00718         verify_len(count + len, "count + std::distance(first, last)");
00719         const size_t affected_elements = end() - where;
00720         if (len < affected_elements)
00721         {
00722           pointer new_last = std::uninitialized_move(
00723               (end() - len).unwrap(), end().unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00724           std::move_backward(where.unwrap(), (end() - len).unwrap(),
00725                              end().unwrap());
00726           std::destroy(where.unwrap(), where.unwrap() + len);
00727 
00728           try
00729           {
00730             std::uninitialized_copy(std::move(first), std::move(last),
00731                                     where.unwrap());
00732           }
00733           catch (...)
00734           {
00735             try
00736             {
00737               std::uninitialized_move(where.unwrap() + len,
00738                                       where.unwrap() + 2 * len, where.unwrap());
00739             }
00740             catch (...)
00741             {
00742               std::destroy(where.unwrap() + len, new_last);
00743               count = where - begin();
00744               throw;
00745             }
00746             std::move(where.unwrap() + 2 * len, new_last, where.unwrap() + len);
00747             std::destroy(end().unwrap(), new_last);
00748             throw;
00749           }
00750         }
00751         else
00752         {
00753           pointer new_loc = where.unwrap() + len;
00754           pointer new_last =
00755               std::uninitialized_move(where.unwrap(), end().unwrap(), new_loc);
00756           std::destroy(where.unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00757 
00758           try
00759           {
00760             std::uninitialized_copy(std::move(first), std::move(last),
00761                                     where.unwrap());
00762           }
00763           catch (...)
00764           {
00765             try
00766             {
00767               std::uninitialized_move(new_loc, new_last, where.unwrap());
00768             }
00769             catch (...)
00770             {
00771               std::destroy(new_loc, new_last);
00772               count = where - begin();
00773               throw;
00774             }
00775             std::destroy(new_loc, new_last);
00776             throw;
00777           }
00778         }
00779         count += len;
00780       }
00781       return where;
00782     }
00783 
00784     iterator insert(iterator where, std::initializer_list<T> list)
00785     {
00786       return insert(where, list.begin(), list.end());
00787     }
00788 
00789     iterator
00790         erase(iterator where) noexcept(std::is_nothrow_move_assignable_v<T>)
00791     {
00792       std::move((where + 1).unwrap(), end().unwrap(), where.unwrap());
00793       std::destroy_at((end() - 1).unwrap());
00794       --count;
00795       return where;
00796     }
00797 
00798     iterator erase(iterator first, iterator last)
00799     {
00800       if (first != last)
00801       {
00802         const pointer res =
00803             std::move(last.unwrap(), end().unwrap(), first.unwrap());
00804         std::destroy(res, end().unwrap());
00805         count = res - begin().unwrap();
00806       }
00807       return first;
00808     }
00809 
00810     iterator pop_back()
00811     {
00812       --count;
00813       std::destroy_at(end().unwrap());
00814       return end();
00815     }
00816 
00817     template < std::forward_iterator  itr>
00818     void assign(itr first, itr last)
00819     {
00820       const auto len = std::distance(first, last);
00821       if (len)
00822       {
00823         verify_len(len, "std::distance(first, last)");
00824         if (len > count)
00825         {
00826           std::copy_n(first, count, begin().unwrap());
00827           std::advance(first, count);
00828           std::uninitialized_copy(std::move(first), std::move(last),
00829                                   end().unwrap());
00830         }
00831         else
00832         {
00833           pointer new_last =
00834               std::copy(std::move(first), std::move(last), begin().unwrap());
00835           std::destroy(new_last, end().unwrap());
00836         }
00837         count = len;
00838       }
00839       else
00840         clear();
00841     }
00842 
00843     void assign(std::initializer_list<T> list)
00844     {
00845       assign(list.begin(), list.end());
00846     }
00847 
00848     void assign(const size_t new_size, const_reference value)
00849     {
00850       if (new_size)
00851       {
00852         verify_len(new_size, "new_size");
00853         if (new_size > count)
00854         {
00855           std::fill(begin().unwrap(), end().unwrap(), value);
00856           std::uninitialized_fill_n(end().unwrap(), new_size - count, value);
00857         }
00858         else
00859         {
00860           pointer new_last = std::fill_n(begin().unwrap(), new_size);
00861           std::destroy(new_last, end().unwrap());
00862         }
00863         count = new_size;
00864       }
00865       else
00866         clear();
00867     }
00868 
00869     void resize(const size_t new_size)
00870     {
00871       if (new_size != count)
00872       {
00873         if (new_size > count)
00874         {
00875           verify_len(new_size, "new_size");
00876           std::uninitialized_value_construct_n(end().unwrap(),
00877                                                new_size - count);
00878         }
00879         else
00880           std::destroy((begin() + new_size).unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00881         count = new_size;
00882       }
00883     }
00884 
00885     void resize(const size_t new_size, const_reference value)
00886     {
00887       if (new_size != count)
00888       {
00889         if (new_size > count)
00890         {
00891           verify_len(new_size, "new_size");
00892           std::uninitialized_fill_n(end().unwrap(), new_size - count, value);
00893         }
00894         else
00895           std::destroy((begin() + new_size).unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00896         count = new_size;
00897       }
00898     }
00899 
00900     void swap(static_vector& other)
00901     {
00902       if (this != &other)
00903       {
00904         if (other.count > count)
00905         {
00906           std::swap_ranges(begin().unwrap(), end().unwrap(),
00907                            other.begin().unwrap());
00908           std::move((other.begin() + count).unwrap(), other.end().unwrap(),
00909                     end().unwrap());
00910           std::destroy((other.begin() + count).unwrap(), other.end().unwrap());
00911         }
00912         else if (other.count < count)
00913         {
00914           std::swap_ranges(other.begin().unwrap(), other.end().unwrap(),
00915                            begin().unwrap());
00916           std::move((begin() + other.count).unwrap(), end().unwrap(),
00917                     other.end().unwrap());
00918           std::destroy((begin() + other.count).unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00919         }
00920         else
00921           std::swap_ranges(begin().unwrap(), end().unwrap(),
00922                            other.begin().unwrap());
00923         std::swap(count, other.count);
00924       }
00925     }
00926 
00927     static_vector& operator=(const static_vector& other)
00928     {
00929       if (this != &other)
00930         assign(other.begin().unwrap(), other.end().unwrap());
00931       return *this;
00932     }
00933 
00934     static_vector& operator=(static_vector&& other) noexcept(
00935         std::is_nothrow_move_assignable_v<T> &&
00936         std::is_nothrow_move_constructible_v<T>)
00937     {
00938       if (this != &other)
00939       {
00940         if (other.count > count)
00941         {
00942           std::move(other.begin().unwrap(), (other.begin() + count).unwrap(),
00943                     begin().unwrap());
00944           std::uninitialized_move((other.begin() + count).unwrap(),
00945                                   other.end().unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00946         }
00947         else
00948         {
00949           std::move(other.begin().unwrap(), other.end().unwrap(),
00950                     begin().unwrap());
00951           std::destroy((begin() + other.count).unwrap(), end().unwrap());
00952         }
00953         count = other.count;
00954         other.clear();
00955       }
00956       return *this;
00957     }
00958 
00959     static_vector& operator=(std::initializer_list<T> list)
00960     {
00961       assign(list.begin(), list.end());
00962       return *this;
00963     }
00964   };
00965 
00966   namespace helpers
00967   {
00968     template <bool are_same, typename... types>
00969     struct enforce_same
00970     {
00971       static_assert(are_same, "static_vector: deduction guide requires all "
00972                               "types during initialization to be the same");
00973     };
00974 
00975     template <typename first, typename... rest>
00976     struct enforce_same<true, first, rest...>
00977     {
00978       typedef remove_cvref_t<first> type;
00979     };
00980 
00981     template <typename first, typename... rest>
00982     using enforce_same_t = typename enforce_same<
00983         (std::is_same_v<remove_cvref_t<first>, remove_cvref_t<rest>> && ...),
00984         first, rest...>::type;
00985   } // namespace helpers
00986 
00987   template <typename first, typename... rest>
00988   static_vector(first, rest...)
00989       -> static_vector<helpers::enforce_same_t<first, rest...>,
00990                        sizeof...(rest) + 1>;
00991 } // namespace alterhook::utils
00992 
00993 namespace std
00994 {
00995 
00996   template <typename T, size_t size>
00997   struct pointer_traits<
00998       alterhook::utils::helpers::static_vector_const_iterator<T, size>>
00999   {
01000     typedef alterhook::utils::helpers::static_vector_const_iterator<T, size>
01001                       pointer;
01002     typedef const T   element_type;
01003     typedef ptrdiff_t difference_type;
01004 
01005     static constexpr element_type* to_address(const pointer itr) noexcept
01006     {
01007       return itr.unwrap();
01008     }
01009   };
01010 
01011   template <typename T, size_t size>
01012   struct pointer_traits<
01013       alterhook::utils::helpers::static_vector_iterator<T, size>>
01014   {
01015     typedef alterhook::utils::helpers::static_vector_iterator<T, size> pointer;
01016     typedef T         element_type;

00463 // Note: `utils_expand` followed by `(~)` is a stupid hack for msvc traditional
00464 // preprocessor to stop complaining about an empty space being passed as an
00465 // argument. Basically if the attribute we are looking for isn't found and
00466 // therefore the stuff in the middle will be replaced with nothing then
00467 // `utils_expand` will leave `~` behind as a result. If found then
00468 // `utils_expand` will be "invoked" with empty parentheses and `(~)` will be
00469 // erased with `utils_del`
00470 #define utils_get_attribute(category, attribute_name, ...)                     \

00664 // clang-format off
00665 /* This generates an exception class using the following properties:
00666  * `exception_name`:
00667  * | The name of the exception (it will therefore be the name of the class
00668  * | generated).
00669  *
00670  * `base`:
00671  * | The base class of the exception (e.g. std::exception). This is not
00672  * | optional.
00673  *
00674  * `__VA_ARGS__`:
00675  * | A list of 0 or more of the following attributes:
00676  * | - stdattr(attribute): Puts `attribute` right after the class keyword and
00677  * |   can therefore be used to trigger implementation defined behavior (e.g.
00678  * |   stdattr([[gnu::visibility("default")]]))
00679  * | - fields(...): A list of pairs or 3-element tuples that specify the fields
00680  * |   of the exception class. They consist of the type of the field, the name
00681  * |   and optionally a keyword named hidden. This makes sure to define each
00682  * |   field in private scope as well as generate a constructor that initializes
00683  * |   those fields with its arguments. If the `hidden` keyword isn't specified
00684  * |   then a getter will also be generated that accesses the specific field.
00685  * |   Note that the prefix `m_` is added on the field names to prevent
00686  * |   shadowing of custom constructor arguments. (e.g. fields((int,
00687  * |   member1), (float, member2, hidden))).
00688  * | - base_args(...): A list of pairs that specify the arguments that the base
00689  * |   class constructor expects. They consist of the type and name of the
00690  * |   arguments. This will add them at the beginning of the current exception's
00691  * |   constructor and will make sure to forward them to the base class as
00692  * |   needed. (e.g. base_args((int, arg1), (float, arg2))).
00693  * | - reason(str): Generates an overload of the `what()`
00694  * |   method of the `std::exception` class which returns `str`.
00695  * | - extra(...): Any extra stuff to be added to the class. They can be method
00696  * |   declarations/definitions, static members etc. They are put in public
00697  * |   scope by default and right after any code generated from the attributes
00698  * |   above. (e.g. extra(void myvfunc() const override;)).
00699  */
00700 #define utils_generate_exception(exception_name, base, ...)                    \
00701                                                                                \
00702                                                                                \
00703                                                                                \
00704                                                                                \
00705                                                                                \
00706                                                                                \
00707                                                                                \
